  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>In <a href="https://issues.apache.org/jira/browse/SOLR-215" title="Multiple Solr Cores - remove static singleton" class="issue-link" data-issue-key="SOLR-215"><del>SOLR-215</del></a>, we enabled support for more then one SolrCore - but there is no way to use them yet.</p> 
                  <p>We need to make some interface to manage, register, modify avaliable SolrCores</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI feel like the suggested implementation is a re-imagining of the Tomcat Manager REST api (\u003ca href=\\\"http:\\/\\/tomcat.apache.org\\/tomcat-6.0-doc\\/manager-howto.html\\\" class=\\\"external-link\\\" rel=\\\"nofollow\\\"\u003ehttp:\\/\\/tomcat.apache.org\\/tomcat-6.0-doc\\/manager-howto.html\u003c\\/a\u003e). The main reason I like the idea of multiple cores in the same instance is to provide tighter integration between them: more like a conventional relational database, with multiple tables that have independent schemas (where Solr core == SQL table). Otherwise, having your servlet container managing the contexts just makes more sense, since that is what it is built for.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAlso, I think the core should be a parameter of the query, so that there is the possibility of querying multiple cores simultaneously. Having a top-level controller managing dispatch to the cores opens up all kinds of possibilities for future expansion, (such as joins between indexes?) and it would make things like federated search much more elegant. \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/SOLR-303\\\" title=\\\"Distributed Search over HTTP\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"SOLR-303\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eSOLR-303\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e already has a \\\"shards\\\" parameter with the same idea behind it: just prefix local cores with the @ symbol, and you are good to go.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eLoving the potential here!\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"stuhood\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12529628_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=stuhood\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"stuhood\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Stu Hood\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12529628_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Sep\\/07 07:31\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2007-09-22T07:31:24+0000\'\u003e22\\/Sep\\/07 07:31\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I feel like the suggested implementation is a re-imagining of the Tomcat Manager REST api ( http:\\/\\/tomcat.apache.org\\/tomcat-6.0-doc\\/manager-howto.html ). The main reason I like the idea of multiple cores in the same instance is to provide tighter integration between them: more like a conventional relational database, with multiple tables that have independent schemas (where Solr core == SQL table). Otherwise, having your servlet container managing the contexts just makes more sense, since that is what it is built for. \\n\\n Also, I think the core should be a parameter of the query, so that there is the possibility of querying multiple cores simultaneously. Having a top-level controller managing dispatch to the cores opens up all kinds of possibilities for future expansion, (such as joins between indexes?) and it would make things like federated search much more elegant.   SOLR-303   already has a \\\"shards\\\" parameter with the same idea behind it: just prefix local cores with the @ symbol, and you are good to go. \\n\\n Loving the potential here! \'core\' used a a name to point to coreA and as an alias to point to coreB)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n1 - One core has one unique immutable name (rename command has been neutralized)\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n2 - existing alias but fails to override a core name.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n   3.2 - unalias(str); if str is a core name identifier, all its aliases get deleted, if str is an alias identifer only that alias gets deleted.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n4 - Core addressing through URLs\\/API can use either name or alias (although using alias is best practice for common \u003cdel\u003eaka non-admin\u003c\\/del\u003e class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003ehey guys ... i\'m catching up on some Jira reading and this comment jumped out at me...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eimproved code related to configuration wrt absolute\\/relative locations: allows core dataDir\\/instanceDir to be absolute or relative to multicore (pseudo) instanceDir\\/dataDir.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e(i\'m guessing that\'s what the dataDir option in the &lt;multicore\\/&gt; tag in Ryan\'s example is for?)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ethis seems like a bad idea to me ... violating the principle of least suprise and all.  it will make the behavior of a solrconfig.xml file dependent on whether or not it\'s being used in a multicore context or not.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'d like to suggest that an aternate approach would be to generalize the current system property based variable substitution to support arbitrary key=val pairs specified when the SolrCore is constructed...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ewe add new syntax to multicore.xml for declaring \\\"global properties\\\"\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eMultiCore converts these global declarations into a SolrParams instance\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ewe also add syntax to multicore.xml for declaring properties specific to a core.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ewhen MultiCore instantiates a core, it uses DefaultSolrParams to let the specific properties override the global properties \u003cb\u003eand\u003c\\/b\u003e to set a special property containing the name of the core (ie: \\\"solr.core.name\\\")\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eif cloning a core is possible (i can\'t remember) MultiCore would reuse the SolrParams from the source core, changing only the core name property (solr.core.name)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003esystem properties with the same names as properties in multicore.xml would trump anything from the configs (since they are a run time overrides)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003e&lt;multicore adminPath=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003etrue\u003c\\/span\u003e\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e &gt;\\n    &lt;requestParsers enableRemoteStreaming=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"\u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003efalse\u003c\\/span\u003e\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e multipartUploadLimitInKB=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"2048\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e \\/&gt;\\n  &lt;\\/requestDispatcher&gt;\\n  &lt;property name=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"alldata.dir\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e&gt;\\/my\\/solr\\/basedir&lt;\\/property&gt;\\n  &lt;property name=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"magicnumber\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e&gt;32&lt;\\/property&gt;\\n\\n  &lt;!-- core0 gets props above, any other props in it\'s configs must come from system props --&gt;\\n  &lt;core name=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"core0\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e instanceDir=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"core0\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e \\/&gt;\\n  &lt;core name=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"core1\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e instanceDir=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"core1\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e&gt;\\n     &lt;property name=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"dataDir\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e&gt;foo&lt;\\/property&gt;\\n  &lt;\\/core&gt;\\n  &lt;core name=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"core111\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e instanceDir=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"core1\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e&gt;&lt;!-- note same instanceDir as above--&gt;\\n     &lt;!-- can reuse exact same instance dir as another core ${solr.core.name} will be differnet --&gt;\\n     &lt;property name=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"dataDir\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e&gt;bar&lt;\\/property&gt;\\n     &lt;!-- and now ${dataDir} will be different too --&gt;\\n  &lt;\\/core&gt;\\n&lt;\\/multicore&gt;\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003eThis would not only give us the ability to have a common ${alldata.dir} for all cores, but also an easy way to reuse the same solrconfig.xml for multiple cores and still get subtle changes in behavior &#8211; all while making it transparent what any one solrconfig.xml will do.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSuper powerful &#8211; and (i think) pretty easy to implement... a new optional SolrParams arg to the SolrCore, SolrConfig, and Config constructors, and added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12562834_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'26\\/Jan\\/08 07:36\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-01-26T07:36:36+0000\'\u003e26\\/Jan\\/08 07:36\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    hey guys ... i\'m catching up on some Jira reading and this comment jumped out at me... \\n\\n  improved code related to configuration wrt absolute\\/relative locations: allows core dataDir\\/instanceDir to be absolute or relative to multicore (pseudo) instanceDir\\/dataDir.  \\n\\n (i\'m guessing that\'s what the dataDir option in the &lt;multicore\\/&gt; tag in Ryan\'s example is for?) \\n\\n this seems like a bad idea to me ... violating the principle of least suprise and all.  it will make the behavior of a solrconfig.xml file dependent on whether or not it\'s being used in a multicore context or not. \\n\\n I\'d like to suggest that an aternate approach would be to generalize the current system property based variable substitution to support arbitrary key=val pairs specified when the SolrCore is constructed... \\n\\n \\n\\t we add new syntax to multicore.xml for declaring \\\"global properties\\\" \\n\\t MultiCore converts these global declarations into a SolrParams instance \\n\\t we also add syntax to multicore.xml for declaring properties specific to a core. \\n\\t when MultiCore instantiates a core, it uses DefaultSolrParams to let the specific properties override the global properties  and  to set a special property containing the name of the core (ie: \\\"solr.core.name\\\") \\n\\t if cloning a core is possible (i can\'t remember) MultiCore would reuse the SolrParams from the source core, changing only the core name property (solr.core.name) \\n\\t system properties with the same names as properties in multicore.xml would trump anything from the configs (since they are a run time overrides) \\n \\n\\n\\n  \\n &lt;multicore adminPath= \\\"\\/admin\\/multicore\\\"  persistent= \\\" true \\\"  &gt;\\n  &lt;abortOnConfigurationError&gt; true &lt;\\/abortOnConfigurationError&gt;\\n  &lt;requestDispatcher handleSelect= \\\" true \\\"  &gt;\\n    &lt;requestParsers enableRemoteStreaming= \\\" false \\\"  multipartUploadLimitInKB= \\\"2048\\\"  \\/&gt;\\n  &lt;\\/requestDispatcher&gt;\\n  &lt;property name= \\\"alldata.dir\\\" &gt;\\/my\\/solr\\/basedir&lt;\\/property&gt;\\n  &lt;property name= \\\"magicnumber\\\" &gt;32&lt;\\/property&gt;\\n\\n  &lt;!-- core0 gets props above, any other props in it\'s configs must come from system props --&gt;\\n  &lt;core name= \\\"core0\\\"  instanceDir= \\\"core0\\\"  \\/&gt;\\n  &lt;core name= \\\"core1\\\"  instanceDir= \\\"core1\\\" &gt;\\n     &lt;property name= \\\"dataDir\\\" &gt;foo&lt;\\/property&gt;\\n  &lt;\\/core&gt;\\n  &lt;core name= \\\"core111\\\"  instanceDir= \\\"core1\\\" &gt;&lt;!-- note same instanceDir as above--&gt;\\n     &lt;!-- can reuse exact same instance dir as another core ${solr.core.name} will be differnet --&gt;\\n     &lt;property name= \\\"dataDir\\\" &gt;bar&lt;\\/property&gt;\\n     &lt;!-- and now ${dataDir} will be different too --&gt;\\n  &lt;\\/core&gt;\\n&lt;\\/multicore&gt;\\n \\n  \\n This would not only give us the ability to have a common ${alldata.dir} for all cores, but also an easy way to reuse the same solrconfig.xml for multiple cores and still get subtle changes in behavior &#8211; all while making it transparent what any one solrconfig.xml will do. \\n\\n Super powerful &#8211; and (i think) pretty easy to implement... a new optional SolrParams arg to the SolrCore, SolrConfig, and Config constructors, and DOMUtil.substituteSystemProperties plus some code in MultiCore to create the SolrParams (hmm,  DOMUtil doesn\'t have a very friendly method for that yet, not that big a deal though) \\n\\n what do you think?              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-12562835\\\" the disconnect ... My understanding based on your early comment was that &lt;multicore dataDir=\\\"...\\\"&gt; was the directory that the &lt;dataDir&gt;...&lt;\\/dataDir&gt; options in each solrconfig.xml would be relative to ...do you mean that in the multicore.xml file, each &lt;core\\/&gt; can have a dataDir option? ... if so that doesn\'t really solve the concern I have: people should be able to read a solrconfig.xml and understand when there are outside inflluences on that config...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003ePlus it could be argued that it increases the element of surprise or at least the potential for side effects.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eIf a solrconfig\\/schema refers to a variable that can be superseded in a multicore.xml, the behavior of a core is explictly dependant on whether it is loaded in a multicore configuration of not. I agree that being explicit rather than implicit is better but this does modify behavior even deeper nevertheless.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI disagree ... it\'s true that using a \\\"variables\\\" approach the evaluation of a solrconfig.xml would be dependent on the environment it\'s run in (ie: is there a multicore.xml? are variables set in it? are any system properties set?) but the evaluation of solrconfog.xml is already dependent on it\'s environment  (ie: what is the solr home? are any system properties set?) ...  my point is that when a human is \u003cb\u003ereading\u003c\\/b\u003e a config with variables in it, it is crystal clear that there is an environmental factor that will affect the behavior.  If a person reads a solrconfig.xml that contains this line...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003e&lt;dataDir&gt;${my.special.dir}\\/data&lt;\\/dataDir&gt;\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003cp\u003e...then it\'s very obvious that the location of the data will depends on the environment the core is run in (in which \\\"my.special.dir\\\" must be set, either as a system property or as a multicore.xml variable &#8211; the point being it\'s an \u003cb\u003eknown\u003c\\/b\u003e external factor).  The approach you guys have been talking about though (assuming i\'m understanding it correctly) would take away that transparency &#8211; people could look at a solrconfig.xml that looks like this...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e&lt;dataDir&gt;data&lt;\\/dataDir&gt;\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e...and that that could mean anything depending on whether or not this solrconfig.xml is running in a multicore setup or not.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"hossman\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12564212_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=hossman\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"hossman\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Hoss Man\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12564212_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'30\\/Jan\\/08 23:16\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-01-30T23:16:49+0000\'\u003e30\\/Jan\\/08 23:16\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I agree generalizing variables is somewhat significant, and a larger scope then just what\'s being talked about here &#8211; perhaps that\'s part of the disconnect ... If we stop\\/start the container, since nothing physically persistent depended on the name, variable substitution (or implicit expansion) can not interfere.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nIf we are using the core \u003cb\u003ename\u003c\\/b\u003e to build data directories, issuing swap is likely to break something...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ePlease correct me if I\'m deeply misunderstanding something...\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"henrib\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12569146_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=henrib\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"henrib\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Henri Biestro\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12569146_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'15\\/Feb\\/08 00:27\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-02-15T00:27:41+0000\'\u003e15\\/Feb\\/08 00:27\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    We need a way to define a global data root without having to define a system env variable; can\'t we at least reintroduce the dataDir as a multicore attribute? \\nThe previous patch version went too far and was ignoring the solrconfig.xml dataDir specification, but having no way to describe where all data go easily is really too inconvenient. \\nCan\'t we find something acceptable in between ? \\nStrawman solution would be, if dataDir is  not  specified in solrconfig.xml, use the previous patch code ? \\nHopefully more acceptable, only provide a minimum set of variables with no possibility to define any for now ? The env would only contain \'solr.multicore. \\n{home,data}\\n \' and for each core,\'solr.multicore.core.instance\' (I\'m reluctant to expose \'sol.multicore.core.name\', explanation follows...) \\n\\n This would not preclude extending variables later and would not delay solr-350 by much now. \\n\\n We used  &lt;dataDir&gt;${solr.data}\\/corename\\/&lt;\\/dataDir&gt;  to illustrate the variable solution but I grow feeling uneasy seeing the core  name  as a variable part of a path (explicit or implicit): if we issue a SWAP command, how do we end up in a proper state when we stop\\/start the container without swapping the directory contents as well ? \\n\\n My rationale is that the  instanceDir  is really what physically identifies a core in a persistent manner wrt SWAP\\/stop\\/start; when we specify a data root, the data directory should somehow depend on the instanceDir as well. \\nFor instance, with  &lt;core name=\\\"books\\\" instanceDir=\\\"books,0\'...\\/&gt;  and  &lt;core name=\\\"books-dev\\\" instanceDir=\\\"books,1\\\"...\\/&gt;  ; even if both use the same data root  \'\\/solr\\/data\' , the \'books\' core will use  \'\\/solr\\/data\\/books,0\\/\'  as dataDir and \'books-dev\' will use  \'\\/solr\\/data\\/books,1\' . \\nWhen we swap(\'books\', \'books-dev\') , everything is still ok; \'books\' now refers to_\'\\/solr\\/data\\/books,1\'_ and books-dev refers to  \'\\/solr\\/data\\/books,0\\/\'  . If we stop\\/start the container, since nothing physically persistent depended on the name, variable substitution (or implicit expansion) can not interfere. \\nIf we are using the core  name  to build data directories, issuing swap is likely to break something... \\n\\n Please correct me if I\'m deeply misunderstanding something...              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eI haven\'t followed the patches, and I quickly read through the last month\'s worth of comments here.  One thing that Hoss said caught my attention:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e\\\"...easy way to reuse the same solrconfig.xml for multiple cores and still\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nget subtle changes in behavior - all while making it transparent what\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nany one solrconfig.xml will do...\\\"\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ePlease count this as my +1 for this.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nYes, one use case is that each core is unique and thus needs unique configs, but I also have a concrete use case where all cores are identical as far as the configs go, all that needs to be different is the data directory where the index lives.  In this case, it would be ideal if one could have a single copy of the schema.xml and solrconfig.xml, and specify core-specific settings (e.g. data\\/index dir) in multicore.xml.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt would be even better if configs for cores were not all in a single\\/monolithic file - imagine a situation where you have thousands or even tends of thousands of indices and you add a few hundred or a few thousand new ones every day, throughout the day.  You could certainly regenerate the whole multicore.xml file every time a new index is added, but it would be much more efficient to generate just the descriptor for that single new index that was just created, and tell Solr - \\\"hey, look here, there is a new core\\/index you need to be aware of\\\".  Perhaps one way to deal with this is to expose an API (URL) to send such a \\\"hey, look here....\\\" message to Solr, and let Solr periodically write out multicore.xml to disk.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"otis\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_12571282_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=otis\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"otis\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Otis Gospodnetic\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_12571282_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'22\\/Feb\\/08 05:55\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2008-02-22T05:55:42+0000\'\u003e22\\/Feb\\/08 05:55\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I haven\'t followed the patches, and I quickly read through the last month\'s worth of comments here.  One thing that Hoss said caught my attention: \\n\\n \\\"...easy way to reuse the same solrconfig.xml for multiple cores and still \\nget subtle changes in behavior - all while making it transparent what \\nany one solrconfig.xml will do...\\\" \\n\\n Please count this as my +1 for this. \\nYes, one use case is that each core is unique and thus needs unique configs, but I also have a concrete use case where all cores are identical as far as the configs go, all that needs to be different is the data directory where the index lives.  In this case, it would be ideal if one could have a single copy of the schema.xml and solrconfig.xml, and specify core-specific settings (e.g. data\\/index dir) in multicore.xml. \\n\\n It would be even better if configs for cores were not all in a single\\/monolithic file - imagine a situation where you have thousands or even tends of thousands of indices and you add a few hundred or a few thousand new ones every day, throughout the day.  You could certainly regenerate the whole multicore.xml file every time a new index is added, but it would be much more efficient to generate just the descriptor for that single new index that was just created, and tell Solr - \\\"hey, look here, there is a new core\\/index you need to be aware of\\\".  Perhaps one way to deal with this is to expose an API (URL) to send such a \\\"hey, look here....\\\" message to Solr, and let Solr periodically write out multicore.xml to disk.
